Let me read it again: "A whirligig spins at five times the speed of a thingamabob. A whatchamacallit spins eleven times faster than a thingamabob. A whatchamacallit spins at 121 meters per second. How fast does a whirligig spin? Why the correct answer is: [27]?"

Alright, so let's break this down. There are three objects: whirligig, thingamabob, and whatchamacallit. Each has a spinning speed, and we need to find the speed of the whirligig.

First, let's assign variables to each to make it easier. Let me denote:

- Let \( V_t \) be the speed of a thingamabob.
- Let \( V_w \) be the speed of a whatchamacallit.
- Let \( V_h \) be the speed of a whirligig.

Now, according to the problem:

1. A whirligig spins at five times the speed of a thingamabob.
2. A whatchamacallit spins eleven times faster than a thingamabob.
3. A whatchamacallit spins at 121 meters per second.

So, translating these into equations:

1. \( V_h = 5 \times V_t \)
2. \( V_w = 11 \times V_t \)
3. \( V_w = 121 \) m/s

Since from equation 3, we know \( V_w \) is 121 m/s, and from equation 2, \( V_w = 11 \times V_t \), we can set them equal to each other:

\( 11 \times V_t = 121 \) m/s

So, to find \( V_t \), we can divide both sides by 11:

\( V_t = \frac{121}{11} \) m/s

Let me calculate that: 121 divided by 11. Hmm, 11 times 11 is 121, so \( V_t = 11 \) m/s.

Now that we have \( V_t \), we can find \( V_h \) from equation 1:

\( V_h = 5 \times V_t = 5 \times 11 = 55 \) m/s
